## Phase 5 — Enemy & Spawner System (~45 files)

### File List

**Enemy Core (~8 files)**
- `Enemy.cs`, `EnemyData.cs` (ScriptableObject)
- `LightTower/EnemyMovement.cs`, `LightTower/EnemyController.cs`
- `EnemyAnimationComponent.cs`
- `EnemyHealthBar.cs`, `EnemyHitVFX.cs`, `EnemySpawnVFX.cs`, `EnemySpawnVFX_mushroom.cs`
- `EnemyGameplayEffectUI.cs`

**Enemy Abilities (~6 files)**
- `EnemyAbility.cs` (abstract, extends AutoAttack)
- `EnemyAbility_applyGE.cs`, `EnemyAbility_spawnEnemies.cs`, `EnemyAbility_targeting.cs`
- `EnemyAICondition.cs` (abstract), `EnemyAICondition_health.cs`, `EnemyAICondition_proximity.cs`

**Spawner Framework (~10 files)**
- `Spawner.cs`, `SpawnerConfig.cs` (ScriptableObject), `SpawnerConfigAutoConfig.cs`
- `FSpawnerConfigAutoConfigData.cs`
- `SpawnerPosition.cs` (abstract), `SpawnerPosition_Circle.cs`, `SpawnerPosition_Line.cs`
- `SpawnerPosition_PathTile.cs`, `SpawnerPosition_FixedPositions.cs`
- `BaseSpawnerData.cs`, `GridBasedSpawnerData.cs`, `CircleBasedSpawnerData.cs`, `PathBasedSpawnerData.cs`

**Wave/Round System (~8 files)**
- `WaveSpawner.cs`, `WaveSpawnerConfig.cs`, `WaveEnemyData.cs`
- `WaveSpawnerConfig_OLD.cs`, `WaveSpawner_OLD.cs`
- `LTSpawner.cs` (round-based spawner)
- `LevelSpawners.cs` (ScriptableObject)
- `TimeSpawner.cs`

**Cycle Management (~5 files)**
- `CyclesManager.cs`, `CycleSpawners.cs` (737 lines — GOD OBJECT, ScriptableObject)
- `SpawnersManager.cs` (singleton)

### What It Looks Like When Running
Enemies spawn in waves/rounds according to cycle configuration. Enemies walk along generated paths toward the player base. Bosses spawn at cycle intervals. Enemies have abilities (apply GE, spawn minions). Health bars visible, hit VFX on damage. Spawner auto-balances difficulty via LpS (Loot per Second) system.

### Difficulty: ★★★ Hard
`CycleSpawners` (737 lines) is a god object that auto-generates spawner configurations with weighted random selection and difficulty balancing. `SpawnersManager` coordinates multiple spawner types (round, wave, time). The LpS auto-balancing formula is the most complex algorithm in the spawner system.

## Phase 6 — Factory & Economy (~40 files)

### File List

**Sources & Resources (~4 files)**
- `Source.cs`, `Resource.cs` (if not in P1)
- `ResourceData.cs` (if not in P0)

**Extractors (~6 files)**
- `Extractor.cs`, `AreaExtractor.cs`
- `ExtractorAudioComponent.cs`, `ExtractorResourceUI.cs`
- `ReachableSourceIndicator.cs`

**Processors (~6 files)**
- `Processor.cs`, `EssenceFactory.cs`
- `ProcessorAudioComponent.cs`, `ProcessorResourceUI.cs`
- `Recipe.cs`, `RecipeElementUI.cs`
- `Producer.cs`

**Conveyor Belt System (~14 files)**
- `ConveyorBelt.cs`, `ConveyorBelt_straight.cs`, `ConveyorBelt_curve.cs`, `ConveyorBelt_storage.cs`
- `ConveyorBeltCombiner.cs`, `ConveyorBeltSplitter.cs`
- `ConveyorBeltCrossing.cs`, `ConveyorBeltUnderground.cs`
- `ConveyorBeltGroup.cs` (409 lines — complex)
- `ConveyorBeltSystem.cs` (singleton)

**Idle Detection (~6 files)**
- `IdleDetector.cs`, `IdleDetector_extractor.cs`, `IdleDetector_processor.cs`
- `IdleManager.cs`, `IdleDetectorButton.cs`, `IdleDetectorUI.cs`

**Player Economy (~4 files)**
- `PlayerData.cs` (447 lines — GOD OBJECT)
- Storage_ResourceData (player inventory)

### What It Looks Like When Running
Complete factory automation loop: extractors mine resources from sources, conveyor belts transport resources through the map (straight, curved, split, merge, underground), processors convert inputs to outputs, storage holds surplus. Idle detection highlights underperforming buildings. Player inventory displays current resources. This is the "Factory" half of "Tower Factory."

### Difficulty: ★★★ Hard
`ConveyorBeltGroup` (409 lines) manages resource transport along connected belt chains with loop detection, merge/split logic, and storage integration. `PlayerData` (447 lines) is a god object tracking all player state. The conveyor belt auto-connection logic in `BuyModeInputMode` (P9) adds cross-phase complexity.

---

## Phase 7 — Special Buildings & Map Objects (~35 files)

### File List

**Beacons (~10 files)**
- `Beacon.cs` (abstract), `CircleBeacon.cs`, `ConeBeacon.cs`, `SquaredBeacon.cs`
- `Beacon_01.cs`, `Beacon_02.cs`, `Beacon_03.cs`, `Beacon_04.cs`

**Crystal/Altar (~4 files)**
- `CrystalAltar.cs`, `CrystalFinder.cs`

**Obelisk (~2 files)**
- `Obelisk.cs`

**Perk Beacon (~4 files)**
- `PerkBeacon.cs`, `PerkBeaconPerk_UI.cs`, `PerkBeaconResourceUI.cs`

**Snowfall (~6 files)**
- `SnowfallBeacon.cs`, `SnowfallBeaconResourceUI.cs`
- `SnowfallController.cs`, `SnowfallControllerUI.cs`
- `SnowfallEffectUI.cs`, `SnowfallVFX.cs`

**Chests (~4 files)**
- `Chest.cs`, `ChestLootTableData.cs`
- `GemsChest.cs`, `GemsChestLootTableData.cs`
- `GoldenCoinsChest.cs`

**Trader (~3 files)**
- `Trader.cs`, `TraderElement.cs`, `TraderElementUI.cs`

**Other (~2 files)**
- `EnemyTower.cs`, `LightBomb.cs`

### What It Looks Like When Running
Map populated with special buildings: fog-clearing beacons (circle, cone, square shapes), crystal altars that grant resources when activated, obelisks that buff adjacent towers, perk beacons that consume resources for upgrades, snowfall beacons that counter weather debuffs, traders that sell items on a cycle timer, chests with gem/gold loot, enemy towers that must be destroyed. Light bombs are throwable damage items.

### Difficulty: ★★☆ Medium
Most special buildings follow a consistent pattern: `GameplayObject` or `MapObject` subclass with `PlacementComponent` events. `SnowfallController` is moderately complex (tracks intensity per cycle, applies tiered debuffs). Beacons are the only deep hierarchy (4 shape variants × 4 named variants).

## Phase 8 — Game Manager & Flow (~30 files)

### File List

**Game Manager (~6 files)**
- `GameManager.cs`, `LTGameManager.cs` (666 lines — GOD OBJECT, abstract)
- `LTGameManager_Campaign.cs`, `LTGameManager_Endless.cs`
- `LTFunctionLibrary.cs` (500 lines — service locator)

**Match & Level (~5 files)**
- `MatchInfo.cs` (singleton), `MatchSettings.cs` (ScriptableObject)
- `LevelData.cs`, `LTLevelController.cs`

**Time & Cycles (~4 files)**
- `TimeManager.cs`, `CyclesManager.cs`
- `DayNightCycle.cs` (405 lines)

**Victory/Defeat (~4 files)**
- `VictoryAnimation.cs`, `BossVictoryAnimation.cs`, `GameOverAnimation.cs`

**Progression (~5 files)**
- `PlayerUpgrade.cs`, `PlayerUpgradesManager.cs` (singleton)
- `LevelsProgressionManager.cs` (singleton)
- `BossReward.cs`, `BossReward_PlayerUpgrade.cs`

**Persistence (~6 files)**
- `SaveSystem.cs` (692 lines — GOD OBJECT)
- `SaveProfile.cs`, `SessionChecker.cs`

### What It Looks Like When Running
Full game loop: main menu → level select → match start → day/night cycles → enemy waves → victory/defeat. Campaign progresses through levels, endless mode runs indefinitely. Day/night transitions change lighting/fog. Time manager controls game speed. Save/load preserves progression. Boss kills grant player upgrades. `LTFunctionLibrary` serves as the central service locator.

### Difficulty: ★★★ Hard
Three god objects: `LTGameManager` (666 lines — game state, economy, tower upgrades), `SaveSystem` (692 lines — reflection-based serialization with BinaryFormatter), `LTFunctionLibrary` (500 lines — facade for ~20 singletons). The save system's use of `BinaryFormatter` + `[Savable]` attribute + `ISavable` interface is the most complex serialization pattern.

---

## Phase 9 — Player & Input (~30 files)

### File List

**Player Controller (~4 files)**
- `PlayerController.cs`, `LTPlayerController.cs` (844 lines — GOD OBJECT)
- `CursorController.cs`

**Input Modes (~4 files)**
- `InputMode.cs` (abstract), `StandardInputMode.cs` (524 lines — GOD OBJECT)
- `EditModeInputMode.cs`, `BuyModeInputMode.cs` (428 lines — GOD OBJECT)

**Camera (~8 files)**
- `IsometricCamera.cs`, `TopCamera.cs`, `SpringArmCamera.cs`
- `PlayerCamera.cs`, `LTCamera.cs`
- `CineMachineArea.cs`, `CineMachineCamera.cs`, `CineMachineSpringArm.cs`
- `CameraShake.cs`, `CameraShakeAnimationEvent.cs`, `ShakeCameraController.cs`

**Hotbar (~5 files)**
- `HotbarController.cs`, `HotbarAction.cs` (abstract)
- `HotbarAction_building.cs`, `HotbarActionUI.cs`, `HotbarUI.cs`

**Wind (~1 file)**
- `WindController.cs`

### What It Looks Like When Running
Player controls isometric camera with zoom/pan/rotate. Three input modes: Standard (select, inspect, sell), Edit (rearrange buildings), Buy (place new buildings with preview + rotation + conveyor auto-connect). Hotbar at bottom with building shortcuts. Cursor changes based on mode/context. Camera shake on explosions.

### Difficulty: ★★★ Hard
Three god objects: `LTPlayerController` (844 lines — largest file in the project), `StandardInputMode` (524 lines), `BuyModeInputMode` (428 lines). The input mode system is the most user-facing code. `BuyModeInputMode` handles conveyor belt auto-connection which cross-references P6 (Factory) heavily.

Tooltips on hover. Pause menu, settings, profile management. End-game screen with stats. Tutorial quest system guides new players. Notifications for important events.

### Difficulty: ★★☆ Medium
High file count but most UI files follow a consistent pattern: subscribe to data events in OnEnable, update display in callbacks, unsubscribe in OnDisable. `SelectableUI_tower` (482 lines) is the only god object — it shows tower stats, upgrade UI, gem management, and target provider selection in one panel.

## Phase 11 — Audio & Polish (~30 files)

### File List

**Audio System (~8 files)**
- `AudioSystem.cs` (456 lines — GOD OBJECT), `AudioData.cs`
- `LTAudioSystem.cs`
- `MusicManager.cs`, `MainMenuMusicManager.cs`, `AmbienceManager.cs`

**Settings (~4 files)**
- `SettingsController.cs` (singleton), `SettingsElement_keyRebind.cs`, `KeyRebindingGroup.cs`

**Stats & Steam (~4 files)**
- `GameStatsManager.cs` (singleton)
- `SteamAchievements.cs` (or equivalent)

**VFX Helpers (~6 files)**
- Various animation event handlers, particle helpers

**Third-Party (read-only, ~8 files)**
- `HighlightPlus/` highlight effects
- `LayerLab/` theme
- `TMPro/` example

### What It Looks Like When Running
Background music transitions between day/night cycles. SFX for all interactions (tower attacks, enemy hits, building placement, UI clicks). Ambient environmental sounds. Steam achievements track player milestones. Settings persist across sessions. Audio source pooling prevents allocation spikes.

### Difficulty: ★☆☆ Easy
`AudioSystem` (456 lines) is the only complex file — it manages source pooling, mixer control, and 2D/3D playback. The rest are event subscribers and wrappers. Steam integration is mostly achievement triggers. Third-party code is read-only.

## Cross-Phase Modification Table

| Phase | Modifies | What Changes | Why |
|-------|----------|------------|-----|
| P3 (Tower) | P2 (Combat) | `TowerCombatComponent` adds `onDamageEnemy` event | Tower-specific damage hooks for GE_ subscriptions |
| P4 (Effects) | P3 (Tower) | GE_ classes subscribe to `TowerCombatComponent.onDamageEnemy` | Effects trigger on tower damage events |
| P4 (Effects) | P2 (Combat) | `GameplayEffectsComponent` modifies `StatsComponent` | Effects apply stat modifiers |
| P5 (Enemy) | P2 (Character) | `Enemy` extends `Character`, `EnemyController` extends `Controller` | Enemy specialization |
| P6 (Factory) | P0 (Core) | `Storage_ResourceData` extends `Storage<T>` | Typed resource storage |
| P6 (Factory) | P1 (Grid) | Conveyor belts reference `GridCell` for placement | Belt snapping to grid |
| P7 (Special) | P4 (Effects) | Beacons/obelisks apply `GameplayEffect` instances | Special building GE application |
| P7 (Special) | P6 (Factory) | `PerkBeacon`, `SnowfallBeacon` consume resources | Resource-activated buildings |
| P8 (Flow) | P3–P7 | `LTGameManager` coordinates buy/sell/upgrade across all systems | Economy orchestration |
| P8 (Flow) | P0–P7 | `SaveSystem` serializes all `ISavable` implementations | Persistence touches everything |
| P9 (Input) | P6 (Factory) | `BuyModeInputMode` auto-connects conveyor belts | Placement logic references belt system |
| P9 (Input) | P8 (Flow) | `LTPlayerController` calls `LTGameManager` for buy/sell | Player actions route through game manager |
| P10 (UI) | P0–P9 | UI subscribes to events from every phase | Display layer for all game systems |
| P11 (Audio) | P0–P9 | Audio triggers on events across all phases | Sound feedback for all actions |

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/twFactory/StructureMap.md ==== -->
# StructureMap — Tower Factory (twFactory)

## Naming Conventions

| Prefix/Suffix | Meaning | Example |
|---------------|---------|---------|
| `SO_` | ScriptableObject data container | `SO_GameplayObjectData`, `SO_LevelData` |
| `Field_` | Management config field | `Field_EStats`, `Field_ResourceType` |
| `W_` | Runtime wrapper (SO → runtime) | `W_GameplayEffect`, `W_SpawnerConfig` |
| `_-System/` | Folder for 3+ tightly coupled files | `_-TowerSystem/`, `_-ConveyorSystem/` |
| `DataService` | Pure C# logic extracted from MonoBehaviour | `DS_ConveyorTransport`, `DS_SpawnerBalance` |
| `I` | Interface | `ISelectable`, `ISavable`, `ISampleableData` |
| `GE_` | Gameplay effect (preserve existing prefix) | `GE_Splash`, `GE_Dot`, `GE_ProjectileBounce` |

---

## Phase 0 — Core Framework & Data

### `_-StatsSystem/` (8 files)
| Current | Becomes | Role |
|---------|---------|------|
| Stat.cs | Stat.cs | Single stat value with modifiers |
| StatConfig.cs | SO_StatConfig.cs | ScriptableObject stat definition |
| StatModifier.cs | StatModifier.cs | Runtime modifier on a stat |
| StatsComponent.cs | StatsComponent.cs | MonoBehaviour stat container, fires `onStatChanged` |
| StatConfigVariable.cs | StatConfigVariable.cs | Variable-based stat config |
| StatConfigObject.cs | StatConfigObject.cs | Object-based stat config |

**DataService candidates:**
- `DS_StatCalculator` — Extract base + modifier math from `StatsComponent` into pure C#. Handles `ModifierOperation` (Add, Multiply, Override) evaluation.

### `_-StorageSystem/` (4 files)
| Current | Becomes | Role |
|---------|---------|------|
| Storage.cs | Storage.cs | Generic `Storage<T>` (Odin SerializedMonoBehaviour) |
| Storage_ResourceData.cs | Storage_ResourceData.cs | Typed resource inventory |
| StorableData.cs | StorableData.cs | Data wrapper |
| Storable.cs | Storable.cs | Storable item interface |

### `_-GameplayObjectBase/` (4 files)
| Current | Becomes | Role |
|---------|---------|------|
| GameplayObject.cs | GameplayObject.cs | Base class for all placeable buildings |
| GameplayObjectData.cs | SO_GameplayObjectData.cs | ScriptableObject definition per building type |
| GameplayObjectDataGroup.cs | SO_GameplayObjectDataGroup.cs | Groups of related building data |
| PlacementComponent.cs | PlacementComponent.cs | Grid placement + events (`onPlace`, `onUnplace`) |

### Standalone files (remaining P0)
- `Cost.cs`, `ResourceData.cs` — data containers (no system needed)
- `FDamageData.cs`, `FDamageReport.cs` — combat data transfer objects
- `FunctionLibrary.cs` — static utility (GOD OBJECT — split candidate)
- `ExtensionMethods.cs`, `RectExtensions.cs` — extension methods
- `Timer.cs`, `RandomizableFloat.cs`, `RandomizableInt.cs`, `WeightedRandomSelector.cs` — utilities
- `LTAssetsReferences.cs` — asset ID registry singleton
- All enum files — standalone
- Serialization surrogates — standalone
- `SavableAttribute.cs`, `ISavable.cs`, `ISelectable.cs`, `ISampleableData.cs` — interfaces
- `SaveComponent.cs` — persistence helper

**DataService candidates:**
- `DS_FunctionLibrary` — Extract pure math/physics from `FunctionLibrary.cs` (586 lines). Physics queries stay in MonoBehaviour wrapper; math/text/validation become pure C#.

**Interface candidates:**
- `ISelectable` — already exists, used by towers, enemies, buildings, map objects
- `ISavable` — already exists, used by save system
- `ISampleableData` — already exists, used by tower data display

**DataService candidates:**
- `DS_PathLayout` — Extract path generation algorithm from `PathGenerator.cs` into pure C#. Input: seed + params → Output: tile positions.
- `DS_EnvironmentPlacement` — Extract spawn probability/position logic from `EnvironmentGenerator.cs` (786 lines). Keep Unity instantiation in MonoBehaviour shell.

## Phase 4 — Gameplay Effects

### `_-GameplayEffects/` (~30 files — keep as single folder)

All GE_ files follow identical pattern: `GE_XxxData.cs` (ScriptableObject) + `GE_Xxx.cs` (runtime). No sub-grouping needed — the `GE_` prefix is the organizing convention.

| Category | Files | Role |
|----------|-------|------|
| Stat modifiers | GE_StatModifier, GE_Slow, GE_SlowResistance | Modify stats (speed, damage, etc.) |
| Damage over time | GE_Dot | Periodic damage ticks |
| Splash/AoE | GE_Splash, GE_SplashDamage | Area damage on hit |
| Chain/Bounce | GE_ProjectileBounce, GE_ProjectileSplit, GE_DirectDamageChain | Multi-target damage propagation |
| Applicators | GE_GameplayEffectApplier, GE_SplashGameplayEffectApplier | Apply other GEs on trigger |
| Stacks | GE_StacksConsumer, GE_StacksConsumerDamage | Consume stacks for burst |
| Healing | GE_Heal, GE_HealLightTower | HP restoration |
| Economy | GE_GiveResources, GE_UnlockBuilding | Resource/unlock rewards |
| Building | GE_GiveEffectToBuilding, GE_GiveEffectToEnemy, GE_DisableTower | Cross-entity effect transfer |
| Utility | GE_AddGemSlot, GE_AreaEffectSpawner, GE_Descriptor, GE_LifeBasedDamage | Misc effects |

### `_-GemSystem/` (3 files)
| Current | Becomes | Role |
|---------|---------|------|
| GemsComponent.cs | GemsComponent.cs | Gem slot container on towers |
| GemData.cs | SO_GemData.cs | Gem definition ScriptableObject |
| GemUI.cs | GemUI.cs | Gem slot display |

**DataService candidates:**
- `DS_EffectStacking` — Extract stack counting, duration refresh, and max-stack capping logic into pure C#. Currently in `GameplayEffectsComponent`.

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/twFactory/SystemPortabilityMap.md ==== -->
# SystemPortabilityMap — Tower Factory (twFactory)

## Classification

- **L0** — Fully portable: Pure C# logic, no Unity dependencies. Can be extracted as standalone library.
- **L1** — Mostly portable: Uses Unity types (Vector3, Quaternion, Color) but no MonoBehaviour lifecycle. Needs thin Unity adapter.
- **L1+** — Partially portable: Uses MonoBehaviour but logic can be separated. Requires refactoring to extract DataService.
- **L2** — Unity-bound: Deep MonoBehaviour/Component dependency. Must remain in Unity project.

---

## Phase 0 — Core Framework & Data

| System | Level | Rationale |
|--------|-------|-----------|
| All enums (EStats, DamageType, etc.) | L0 | Pure enum definitions |
| Stat, StatModifier | L0 | Pure math (add/multiply/override operations) |
| StatsComponent | L1+ | MonoBehaviour container; stat math extractable as DS_StatCalculator |
| StatConfig, StatConfigVariable | L1 | ScriptableObject data; config data is pure |
| Cost, ResourceData | L0 | Pure data containers |
| FDamageData, FDamageReport | L0 | Pure data transfer objects |
| Storage<T>, Storage_ResourceData | L1+ | Odin SerializedMonoBehaviour; dictionary logic is pure |
| GameplayObjectData | L1 | ScriptableObject — data is pure, needs SO adapter |
| GameplayObject | L2 | MonoBehaviour with PlacementComponent, lifecycle |
| PlacementComponent | L2 | MonoBehaviour with grid/collider interaction |
| FunctionLibrary (pure math) | L1 | Uses Vector3/Quaternion but algorithms are pure math |
| FunctionLibrary (physics queries) | L2 | Raycasting, overlap checks — Unity-bound |
| ExtensionMethods, RectExtensions | L0 | Pure C# extensions |
| RandomizableFloat/Int | L0 | Pure random range |
| WeightedRandomSelector | L0 | Pure weighted random algorithm |
| Timer | L0 | Pure time tracking |
| SavableAttribute, ISavable | L0 | Pure attribute/interface |
| Serialization surrogates | L1 | Uses Unity Vector3/Quaternion types |
| LTAssetsReferences | L2 | MonoBehaviour singleton, asset lookups |

## Phase 1 — Grid & Map Generation

| System | Level | Rationale |
|--------|-------|-----------|
| Grid, GridCell | L1+ | Grid data structure is pure; rendering/interaction is Unity |
| Tile, PathTile, Path | L1 | Position data + adjacency graph — uses Vector3 |
| PathChunk | L1 | Path segment data |
| PathGenerator (algorithm) | L1 | Procedural generation algorithm; uses Vector3 positions |
| GroundGenerator, GroundChunk | L2 | Mesh generation, Unity terrain |
| EnvironmentGenerator | L2 | Unity instantiation, scene manipulation |
| MapGenerator | L2 | Orchestrates Unity generators |
| FogOfWarController | L2 | Render texture, camera — deeply Unity-bound |
| FogOfWarArea | L2 | Collider-based area — Unity-bound |
| LevelData | L1 | ScriptableObject config data |
| LevelController, LTLevelController | L2 | MonoBehaviour lifecycle |
| MapObject | L2 | MonoBehaviour base |
| Source, Resource | L2 | MonoBehaviour with colliders |

| TowerCombatComponent | L2 | Tower-specific events + MonoBehaviour |
| EnemyCombatComponent | L2 | Enemy-specific + MonoBehaviour |
| Ability, ActiveAbility, PassiveAbility | L1+ | Abstract logic could be pure; MonoBehaviour for lifecycle |
| AutoAttack | L2 | Requires Unity physics/timing |
| AbilityManager | L1+ | Queue logic is pure; execution needs Unity |
| AbilityQueue, QueuedAbility | L0 | Pure priority queue data structure |
| FActiveAbilityInputData | L0 | Pure data DTO |

| FSMState, FSMCondition, FSMTask, FSMTransition | L0 | Pure state machine definitions |

## Summary

| Level | Count | Description |
|-------|-------|-------------|
| **L0** | ~40 systems | Pure C# — directly extractable |
| **L1** | ~30 systems | Needs thin Unity type adapter |
| **L1+** | ~20 systems | Requires DataService extraction |
| **L2** | ~100+ systems | Unity-bound — stays in project |

### Highest-Value L0 Extractions

1. **DS_ConveyorTransport** — Belt chain traversal, resource distribution, loop detection (from ConveyorBeltGroup)
2. **DS_SpawnerBalance** — LpS auto-balancing formula, weight distribution, duration calculation (from CycleSpawners)
3. **DS_Economy** — Cost evaluation, refund math, resource sufficiency (from LTGameManager)
4. **DS_StatCalculator** — Stat modifier stacking with operation order (from StatsComponent)
5. **DS_Serializer** — Reflection-based [Savable] field discovery, binary encode/decode (from SaveSystem)
6. **DS_RecipeEvaluator** — Input matching, output quantity calculation (from Processor)
7. **DS_TowerExperience** — XP threshold lookup, stat scaling per level (from Tower)
8. **DS_EffectStacking** — Stack counting, duration refresh, max-cap logic (from GameplayEffectsComponent)
9. **DS_PlacementValidator** — Grid occupancy, adjacency rules, belt connectivity (from BuyModeInputMode)
10. **DS_PathLayout** — Procedural path generation algorithm (from PathGenerator)
11. **DS_WaveComposition** — Wave enemy composition, weight selection, boss interval (from CycleSpawners)
12. **DS_SnowfallIntensity** — Per-cycle intensity calculation, tier thresholds (from SnowfallController)

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/twFactory/surfer.md ==== -->
# surfer — Tower Factory (twFactory)

## Prompt 1: Initial source analysis

**Date:** 2025-07-22

**Action:** Full project initialization and source analysis for Tower Factory (twFactory).

**Source Scope:**
- 19,643 total project files (1.568 GB) — from .stub
- 554 game code files in Assembly-CSharp (~49,000 lines)
- 48 compiled DLL assemblies
- 4 scenes: GameScene, LoadingScreen, MainMenu, Tutorial

**Key Findings:**
- Game is Tower Factory — Tower Defense + Factory Automation hybrid
- Unity 6 engine with URP, Input System, Addressables, Localization, Cinemachine
- 11 singletons (GameManager, AudioSystem, SaveSystem, SpawnersManager, FogOfWarController, SettingsController, PlayerUpgradesManager, LevelsProgressionManager, GameStatsManager, ConveyorBeltSystem, MatchInfo)
- Central service locator: `LTFunctionLibrary` — static facade for ~20 manager singletons
- 0 FindObjectOfType calls — clean architecture using singleton registry + LTFunctionLibrary
- 10 god objects (>400 lines): LTPlayerController (844), EnvironmentGenerator (786), CycleSpawners (737), SaveSystem (692), LTGameManager (666), FunctionLibrary (586), StandardInputMode (524), LTFunctionLibrary (500), SelectableUI_tower (482), AudioSystem (456)
- Event-driven architecture using C# delegates/Action<T> (no UnityEvents in game logic)
- 25+ gameplay effect types following consistent GE_ paired pattern (Data SO + Runtime)
- Conveyor belt system with 8 belt variants, group-based resource transport
- 13 tower types × 3 upgrade tiers, 27 enemy types, 10 target provider strategies
- Procedural map generation: PathGenerator → GroundGenerator → EnvironmentGenerator
- Save system uses BinaryFormatter + [Savable] attribute + ISavable interface (security concern noted)

**Documents Generated:**
1. ARCHITECTURE.md — dependency graph, singletons, coupling, events, data flow, inheritance, assets
2. PhaseMap.md — 12 phases with file lists, difficulty ratings, cross-phase modification table
3. StructureMap.md — per-phase system folders, DataService candidates, interface candidates
4. GOAL.md — architecture rules, naming conventions, lifecycle rules, testing strategy
5. Estimate.md — ~585h total (440.5h code + 145h overhead) across 12 phases
6. SystemPortabilityMap.md — L0/L1/L1+/L2 classification, 12 highest-value DataService extractions
7. surfer.md — this file

---

## God Objects

No file exceeds 200 lines. Largest files doing 2+ things:

| File | Lines | Responsibilities | Verdict |
|---|---|---|---|
| `lift.cs` | ~200 | Elevator movement, door animation, audio, lighting, NPC reveal, floor transitions (state machine x=0..23) | **Split candidate** — state machine + door anim + audio should separate |
| `pl.cs` | ~120 | Player movement, mouse look, running, FOV zoom, footstep audio, camera bob animation | **Split candidate** — movement vs camera vs audio |
| `menu.cs` | ~100 | Pause, settings (sensitivity/audio/language), cursor lock, camera toggle | Minor — typical menu |
| `hide.cs` | ~95 | Player hiding, camera transitions, input during hide, exit coroutine | Acceptable |
| `wfcode.cs` | ~100 | Combination lock input, cylinder rotation, door unlock, camera transition | Acceptable |

---

## Singleton Registry

**No formal singletons exist.** All scripts communicate via serialized `public GameObject` references assigned in the Inspector. There are no `static Instance` fields, no `DontDestroyOnLoad`, no service locators.

---

## Coupling Hotspots

### 1. `cam.cs` — Universal Dispatcher via SendMessage + Name-based GetComponent
```csharp
gameObject.GetComponent(gameObject.name).SendMessage("use");
```
This looks up a component **by the GameObject's name** and calls `use()` via SendMessage. Every interactable object must have its script name match its GameObject name. Extremely fragile.

### 2. Direct cross-domain references everywhere
- `lift.cs` directly reads `pl.GetComponent<pl>().cam.GetComponent<tryaska>()` — three levels deep
- `hide.cs` reads `pl.GetComponent<pl>().cam`, `.camm`, `.MX`, `.MY`, `.MZ`
- `wfscare1.cs` writes to `pl.GetComponent<pl>().MX` and `pl.GetComponent<pl>().MY`
- `trigscare.cs` calls `v.GetComponent<vkl>().use()` and `c.GetComponent<cam>().dist`

### 3. Uncached GetComponent calls in Update
Almost every script calls `GetComponent<>()` inside `Update()` or `FixedUpdate()` rather than caching in `Start()`. Examples:
- `dver.cs`: `base.gameObject.GetComponent<AudioSource>()` — called 8+ times per frame
- `cam.cs`: `GetComponent<vkl>()`, `GetComponent<dver>()` per raycast

### 4. Tag-based string comparisons
- `"Player"` tag checked in: cam, addforcescr, trigscare, wfscare1, wfcolis, wfsatr, opttrig, wfkill
- `"slomokno"` tag in cam
- `"wflook"` tag in wfscare2

### 5. `.active` property (deprecated)
Multiple scripts use `.active` instead of `.activeSelf`:
- `fl.active` in wfcode, wfzap
- `aud.active` in wfcode1
- `p.active` in wfcolis

---

## Event System

**None.** The project uses zero events — no `UnityEvent`, no `System.Action`, no `delegate`, no custom event bus.

All communication patterns:
1. **Direct reference + method call**: `l.a()` (liftkn → lift)
2. **SendMessage**: `gameObject.SendMessage("use")` (cam → any interactable)
3. **Direct field read/write**: `pl.GetComponent<pl>().MX = -90f` (wfscare1 → pl)
4. **Coroutine chains**: `StartCoroutine(end())` for delayed sequences

---

## Data Flow

```
Inspector-assigned references (public GameObject fields)
         │
         ▼
   MonoBehaviour.Update()
         │
         ├── Player input → pl (movement/look) → Rigidbody.AddForce
         │
         ├── cam raycast → SendMessage("use") → target script.use()
         │
         ├── Trigger/Collision → OnTriggerEnter → direct calls
         │
         └── State integers (x, on, a) → drive sequential logic
```

- **No ScriptableObjects** for runtime data
- **No data containers** — all state is in-field on MonoBehaviours
- **No save/load system**
- **State machines** use raw `int` fields (e.g., `lift.x`, `wfcode1.on`, `wfscare2.a`)

---

## Inheritance Chains

**Flat hierarchy.** Every script directly extends `MonoBehaviour`. No custom base classes, no interfaces, no abstract classes.

| Class | Base |
|---|---|
| All 38 game scripts | `MonoBehaviour` |
| `Readme` | `ScriptableObject` |
| `SimpleCameraController` | `MonoBehaviour` (Unity template) |

---

## External Packages

| Package/Plugin | Evidence |
|---|---|
| **Unity HDRP** | `Unity.RenderPipelines.HighDefinition.Runtime.dll`, HDRP shaders in Assets, `Volume` component usage in lift.cs |
| **TextMeshPro** | `Unity.TextMeshPro.dll` |
| **Timeline** | `Unity.Timeline.dll` |
| **VFX Graph** | `Unity.VisualEffectGraph.Runtime.dll` |
| **Jemeza SFASFX** | `Jemeza/SFASFX/SoundPlayer.cs` — third-party sound effect player |
| **NavMesh** | `UnityEngine.AIModule.dll` — used by nm.cs, wfkill.cs |

---

## Asset Inventory (from .stub)

### Audio Clips (~60 files, ~90 MB)
Ambient loops, door sounds, footsteps, scares, elevator SFX, heartbeat, breath, siren, dog bark, wind, code beeps. Mix of `.wav` and `.ogg`. Many Russian-named files (dver = door, shagi = footsteps, zvyk = sound, ysilenie = amplification).

### 3D Meshes (~130+ files, `.glb`)
Characters (body, head, eyes, jaw, clothes), furniture (cabinet, stool, shelf, bowl), doors (multiple types including SCP-432 themed), elevator parts, pipes, fire extinguisher, flashlight, tools (crowbar, wrench, axe, hammer, saw), props (cola can, cement bag, radio, bottles), architectural elements. Russian-named meshes present (Дверь = door, Шкаф = cabinet, Куб = cube).

### Textures (~200+ files, `.png`/`.tga`, ~300+ MB)
Albedo, normal, roughness maps for all mesh assets. UI textures (buttons, sliders, toggles). Horror textures (blood, gore, body parts). Game-specific (wanted poster — rozisk, warning signs, panel textures). Largest textures are character body/clothing normals (~6-10 MB each).

### Shaders (~80 files)
Primarily HDRP built-in shaders. HDRP Lit, Decal, deferred tile shading, atmospheric scattering, temporal AA, sky shaders. No custom shaders identified.

### Scenes
Single main scene: `Assets/SceneHierarchyObject/2.glb` (174.77 MB) — entire game in one scene.

### UI Assets
Font: "Perfect DOS VGA 437" (retro CRT aesthetic). Standard Unity UI sprites. Custom button/toggle skins (GUISkin-style).

### Materials & Config
Audio mixers (2), PhysicMaterial (1), NavMesh data, InputManager (legacy input), HDRP quality/graphics settings, PlayerSettings (26.9 KB — full build config).

# GOAL — wrngfloor

## Project Identity

**Wrong Floor** — A first-person horror game built in Unity (HDRP). Player explores a building, solves a combination lock, rides an elevator to the wrong floor, and encounters scripted horror events in a basement level. Single scene, 38 game scripts, ~200 lines max per file.

---

## Target Architecture Rules

### 1. Folder Structure

```
Assets/
├── _-PlayerSystem/
│   ├── PlayerController.cs
│   ├── PlayerLook.cs
│   ├── W_PlayerFootsteps.cs
│   ├── InteractionRaycaster.cs
│   ├── FlashlightController.cs
│   ├── CameraShake.cs
│   └── LookAtTarget.cs
├── _-DoorSystem/
│   ├── PhysicsDoor.cs
│   ├── AnimatedDoor.cs
│   └── KeyPickup.cs
├── _-ElevatorSystem/
│   ├── ElevatorController.cs
│   ├── ElevatorSequence_Descent.cs
│   ├── ElevatorSequence_NPCReveal.cs
│   └── ElevatorButton.cs
├── _-NPCSystem/
│   ├── NPCWalker.cs
│   ├── NPCKillSequence.cs
│   └── NPCScareEvent.cs
├── _-PuzzleSystem/
│   ├── CombinationLock.cs
│   ├── LockInspection.cs
│   └── HidingSpot.cs
├── _-ScareEventSystem/
│   ├── ScareEvent_NPCAppear.cs
│   ├── ScareEvent_ForcedLook.cs
│   ├── ScareEvent_DoorSlam.cs
│   ├── ScareEvent_LightsOut.cs
│   ├── ScareEvent_WrongFloor.cs
│   └── SkullInspection.cs
├── _Interfaces/
│   ├── IInteractable.cs
│   ├── IDoor.cs
│   ├── IScareEvent.cs
│   └── IPlayerState.cs
├── _DataServices/
│   ├── PlayerInputService.cs
│   ├── ElevatorStateMachine.cs
│   └── CombinationLockLogic.cs
├── _ScriptableObjects/
│   ├── SO_PlayerConfig.cs
│   ├── SO_InteractionConfig.cs
│   ├── SO_DoorConfig.cs
│   ├── SO_LightSwitchConfig.cs
│   ├── SO_ElevatorConfig.cs
│   ├── SO_CombinationLockConfig.cs
│   └── SO_GameSettings.cs
├── _Standalone/
│   ├── LightSwitch.cs
│   ├── SimpleLightSwitch.cs
│   ├── AdjustableLamp.cs
│   ├── ObjectToggle.cs
│   ├── SoundTrigger.cs
│   ├── ConditionalActivator.cs
│   ├── HintPopup.cs
│   ├── RoomCulling.cs
│   ├── RoomCullingTrigger.cs
│   ├── MirrorReflection.cs
│   ├── WindAudioFollower.cs
│   ├── DistancePitchController.cs
│   ├── PlayerSmoothnessOverride.cs
│   ├── FrameRateCameraSwap.cs
│   ├── ThirdPersonDeathCam.cs
│   ├── FlashlightPuzzle.cs
│   ├── DarknessFearEffect.cs
│   ├── TriggerActivator.cs
│   ├── CollisionPopup.cs
│   └── WorldObjectShake.cs
└── _UI/
    └── PauseMenu.cs
```

### 2. Naming Conventions

| Element | Convention | Example |
|---|---|---|
| MonoBehaviour (system) | PascalCase, descriptive | `PlayerController`, `PhysicsDoor` |
| MonoBehaviour (wrapper) | `W_` prefix | `W_PlayerFootsteps` |
| Interface | `I` prefix | `IInteractable`, `IDoor` |
| ScriptableObject | `SO_` prefix | `SO_PlayerConfig` |
| DataService | PascalCase, `Service`/`Logic`/`StateMachine` suffix | `ElevatorStateMachine` |
| Private fields | `_camelCase` | `_moveDirection`, `_isRunning` |
| Serialized fields | `[SerializeField] private` | `[SerializeField] private float _speed;` |
| Public API methods | PascalCase, descriptive verbs | `Use()`, `ToggleLight()`, `Call()` |
| Coroutines | PascalCase with descriptive name | `OpenDoorsSequence()`, `FlickerLoop()` |

### 3. Class Responsibilities

**MonoBehaviour scripts must do ONE thing:**
- `PlayerController` → movement only (no camera, no audio)
- `PlayerLook` → mouse look only
- `InteractionRaycaster` → raycast + dispatch only
- `FlashlightController` → flashlight hold/toggle only

**No script should:**
- Directly access another system's private state (no `pl.GetComponent<pl>().MX = -90f`)
- Use `SendMessage()` — use `IInteractable.Use()` instead
- Use `GetComponent(string)` by name — use typed interface
- Call `GetComponent<>()` in `Update()` — cache in `Awake()`/`Start()`

### 4. Decoupling Patterns

#### Replace SendMessage with IInteractable
```csharp
// BEFORE (cam.cs)
gameObject.GetComponent(gameObject.name).SendMessage("use");

// AFTER (InteractionRaycaster.cs)
if (hit.transform.TryGetComponent<IInteractable>(out var interactable))
    interactable.Use();
```

#### Replace direct field writes with interface/events
```csharp
// BEFORE (wfscare1.cs)
pl.GetComponent<pl>().MX = -90f;
pl.GetComponent<pl>().MY = 10f;

// AFTER — via event or interface
public static event System.Action<Vector2> OnForceLookDirection;
OnForceLookDirection?.Invoke(new Vector2(-90f, 10f));

// PlayerLook subscribes
OnForceLookDirection += (dir) => { _mx = dir.x; _my = dir.y; };
```

#### Replace state integers with enums
```csharp
// BEFORE (lift.cs)
public int x; // 0, 1, 2, ... 23

// AFTER
public enum ElevatorState { Idle, Ascending, DoorsOpening, WaitingForPlayer, ... }
private ElevatorState _state = ElevatorState.Idle;
```

#### Cache GetComponent calls
```csharp
// BEFORE (dver.cs) — called 8+ times per frame
base.gameObject.GetComponent<AudioSource>().Play();

// AFTER
private AudioSource _audio;
private void Awake() => _audio = GetComponent<AudioSource>();
private void PlayAudio() => _audio.Play();
```

### 5. Lifecycle Rules

- `Awake()` — cache components, resolve references
- `Start()` — initialize state, subscribe to events
- `OnDestroy()` — unsubscribe from events
- `Update()` — input reading, state checks (no heavy logic)
- `FixedUpdate()` — physics only (`Rigidbody.AddForce`)
- Coroutines — sequenced events with `WaitForSeconds`

### 6. C# Features to Adopt

| Feature | Use Case |
|---|---|
| `enum` | All state machines (elevator, scare events, door states) |
| `[SerializeField] private` | All inspector-assigned fields (replace `public GameObject`) |
| `TryGetComponent<T>()` | Replace `GetComponent<T>() != null` checks |
| `switch` expressions | State machine transitions |
| `readonly` fields | Cached component references |
| `string.Empty` / `nameof()` | Replace magic strings |
| Properties | Replace direct field access for external reads |

### 7. Tags & Layers

**Existing tags (preserve):**
- `Player` — player collider
- `slomokno` — breakable door glass (special interaction path in cam.cs)
- `wflook` — wrong floor look target (raycast check in wfscare2)

**No custom layers identified** — only default physics LayerMasks.

### 8. Testing Strategy

| Level | What to Test | How |
|---|---|---|
| Unit | `CombinationLockLogic` — digit increment, code validation | NUnit, no MonoBehaviour needed |
| Unit | `ElevatorStateMachine` — state transitions | NUnit, pure C# |
| Unit | `PlayerInputService` — input → vector mapping | NUnit with mock input |
| Integration | `IInteractable` dispatch — raycaster finds and calls correct target | PlayMode test with scene setup |
| Integration | Door unlock flow — key pickup → door enabled | PlayMode test |
| Manual | Full horror sequences — timing, audio, camera | Playtest checklist per phase |

### 9. Performance Guidelines

- **Cache all GetComponent calls** — current code calls GetComponent 30+ times per frame across all scripts
- **Room culling** — preserve opt/opttrig system, it's the only optimization
- **Single scene** — no scene splitting needed (project is small)
- **AudioSource pooling** — not needed (low audio source count)
- **No object pooling needed** — no runtime instantiation found

### 10. Migration Order

1. **Phase 1 first** — `pl`, `cam`, `fl` are the foundation everything depends on
2. **Create `IInteractable` interface before Phase 2** — all interactables need it
3. **Phase 2 interactables** adopt `IInteractable` immediately
4. **Phase 3 elevator** — extract state machine, adopt SO config
5. **Phase 4** — straightforward renames, minimal logic changes
6. **Phase 5** — largest phase, but scripts are mostly independent triggers
7. **Phase 6** — menu last, bind to `SO_GameSettings`

# PhaseMap — wrngfloor

## Phase Overview

| Phase | Name | Files | Weight % | Difficulty | Depends On |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Player Core | 5 | 20% | Medium | — |
| 2 | Doors & Switches | 9 | 20% | Low–Medium | Phase 1 |
| 3 | Elevator System | 2 | 15% | Medium–High | Phase 1, 2 |
| 4 | Environment & Optimization | 8 | 10% | Low | Phase 1 |
| 5 | Horror Events & NPC | 16 | 25% | Medium | Phase 1, 2, 4 |
| 6 | UI & Menu | 1 | 10% | Low | Phase 1 |

**Total actionable scripts: 41** (38 game + 2 third-party kept + 1 Readme SO)

---

## Phase 1 — Player Core

**What it does:** First-person player movement, mouse look, camera interaction raycast, flashlight, screen shake.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `pl.cs` | ~120 | Player movement, mouse look, running, footstep audio, camera bob, FOV zoom |
| `cam.cs` | ~40 | Interaction raycast — dispatches `use()` via SendMessage to interactables |
| `fl.cs` | ~85 | Flashlight hold/toggle, follows player aim with sway |
| `tryaska.cs` | ~25 | Camera shake effect (random rotation + flicker) |
| `lookat.cs` | ~8 | Simple LookAt utility component |

### What It Looks Like When Running
Player walks in first-person with WASD, mouse look, running with shift. Flashlight toggles with a key, sways naturally. Pressing "use" button casts a ray and interacts with whatever is hit. Camera can shake when tryaska is enabled.

### Difficulty: Medium
`pl.cs` is the most coupled script in the project — nearly everything reads its fields. `cam.cs` uses fragile name-based GetComponent dispatch. Decoupling these will require an interaction interface.

---

## Phase 2 — Doors & Switches

**What it does:** Physics-based doors, light switches with flicker, key pickups, sound triggers, simple activators.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `dver.cs` | ~105 | Physics hinge door with audio (creak, slam, handle) |
| `vkl.cs` | ~65 | Light switch with random flicker coroutine |
| `vklt.cs` | ~30 | Simple light switch variant (no flicker) |
| `lampa.cs` | ~30 | Adjustable lamp bone rotation |
| `key.cs` | ~35 | Key pickup — unlocks a door, plays animation |
| `klych.cs` | ~20 | Generic switch — activates/deactivates object arrays |
| `sound.cs` | ~25 | Play audio on `use()` |
| `tr.cs` | ~12 | Conditional activator — if vkl is on, activate target |
| `wfpodsk.cs` | ~20 | Hint popup — shows UI element temporarily |

### What It Looks Like When Running
Doors swing open/closed with physics, creak, and slam sounds. Light switches toggle room lights with occasional flicker. Keys can be picked up to unlock specific doors. Interaction hints appear briefly.

### Difficulty: Low–Medium
Most scripts are small and self-contained. `dver.cs` has complex angle math for slam detection but is well-isolated. `vkl.cs` flicker logic uses coroutine ping-pong.

---

## Phase 3 — Elevator System

**What it does:** Multi-floor elevator with doors, descent, lighting changes, and NPC encounter sequence.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `lift.cs` | ~200 | Elevator state machine (x=0..23): call, ascend, open doors, descend, trap player, second descent, NPC reveal, ending |
| `liftkn.cs` | ~12 | Elevator call button — triggers `lift.a()` |

### What It Looks Like When Running
Player presses elevator button. Elevator ascends with motor sounds, doors open. Player enters, doors close. Elevator descends to basement. Doors open to new area. Later, elevator is called again (NPC riding it), descends with shake, doors open for final encounter.

### Difficulty: Medium–High
`lift.cs` is the most complex file — a 23-state sequential machine controlling position, doors, audio, lighting, NPC visibility, camera distance, and coroutines. Tightly coupled to `pl`, `cam`, `tryaska`. Primary god-object split candidate.

---

## Phase 4 — Environment & Optimization

**What it does:** Room culling, mirror reflections, ambient audio positioning, distance-based pitch, camera effects.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `opt.cs` | ~20 | Room activation/deactivation (manual LOD) |
| `opttrig.cs` | ~20 | Trigger zones that increment/decrement room visibility counters |
| `mirror.cs` | ~40 | Real-time mirror — mirrors player model, door, flashlight positions |
| `veter.cs` | ~20 | Wind audio source follows player Z position |
| `audpitch.cs` | ~15 | Distance-based audio pitch controller |
| `wfplavn.cs` | ~8 | One-shot: sets player smoothness value, then self-destructs |
| `kadr25.cs` | ~15 | Frame-rate camera swap (horror low-FPS effect) |
| `Wftpscam.cs` | ~20 | Third-person camera with wall collision raycast |

### What It Looks Like When Running
Rooms activate/deactivate as player moves between zones (performance optimization). A bathroom mirror reflects the player model and flashlight in real-time. Wind sound follows the player through corridors. Certain cameras swap at low frame rates for VHS horror effect.

### Difficulty: Low
All scripts are small and independent. `mirror.cs` has the most math (position/rotation mirroring) but is self-contained.

---

## Phase 5 — Horror Events & NPC

**What it does:** All scripted horror sequences — scare triggers, NPC encounters, combination lock puzzle, hiding mechanic, death sequences, wrong floor event chain.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `wfcode.cs` | ~100 | Combination lock puzzle (4 cylinders, correct code: 1990) |
| `wfcode1.cs` | ~55 | Wrong floor event sequence (audio → footsteps → door open) |
| `wfzap.cs` | ~65 | Lock inspection interaction (camera zoom to lock) |
| `wfkill.cs` | ~45 | NPC kill sequence (NavMesh approach → detect → death animation → game over camera) |
| `nm.cs` | ~20 | NPC NavMesh walk to waypoint |
| `wfscare1.cs` | ~55 | Scare event: NPC animates when player looks, forces camera direction, FOV flash |
| `wfscare2.cs` | ~45 | Scare event: NPC appears when player passes, animates when looked at or player retreats |
| `wfscare2v2.cs` | ~45 | Scare variant: forced look at NPC, flashlight aim, FOV snap |
| `hide.cs` | ~95 | Player hides in furniture — camera transitions, limited look, exit sequence |
| `golova.cs` | ~45 | Head/skull inspection — camera switches to examine, eyes track player |
| `addforcescr.cs` | ~55 | Door slam scare — trigger enters, door slammed by force, FOV flash |
| `trigscare.cs` | ~45 | Trigger scare — lights off via vkl, reduced interaction distance, NPC animation |
| `f.cs` | ~35 | Flashlight puzzle — toggle light reveals hidden objects step by step |
| `f2.cs` | ~35 | Darkness fear effects — voice when flashlight off, periodic heartbeat |
| `wfsatr.cs` | ~18 | Trigger activator — activate/deactivate object arrays on enter |
| `wfcolis.cs` | ~18 | Collision popup — shows message on physics collision |

### What It Looks Like When Running
The game's horror content: combination lock with code 1990 (year-themed). Scripted scares — NPCs appear, doors slam, lights go out. Player can hide in cabinets. An NPC walks toward the player and kills them. Darkness triggers fear audio. The "wrong floor" sequence plays ambient horror sounds with approaching footsteps.

### Difficulty: Medium
Many small self-contained trigger scripts. `wfcode.cs` has the most interactive logic (input handling in camera-locked mode). `wfkill.cs` combines NavMesh + raycast + death sequence. `hide.cs` has complex camera reparenting.

---

## Phase 6 — UI & Menu

**What it does:** Pause menu, settings (sensitivity, audio, language, camera shake toggle), quit.

### File List

| File | Lines | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `menu.cs` | ~100 | Pause menu — sensitivity slider, volume slider, language toggle (RU/EN), camera shake toggle, debug cam, quit |

### What It Looks Like When Running
ESC opens pause menu overlay. Sliders control mouse sensitivity and audio volume. Toggle for camera shake. Language switch between Russian and English (swaps UI GameObjects). L key toggles debug camera. Exit button quits application.

### Difficulty: Low
Single self-contained file. Clear UI binding pattern (Slider/Toggle → public method).

---

## Cross-Phase Modification Table

| Modification | Source Phase | Target Phase | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| `cam.dist` write | Phase 5 (trigscare, lift) | Phase 1 (cam) | Horror events change interaction raycast distance |
| `pl.MX/MY/MZ` write | Phase 5 (wfscare1, wfscare2v2, hide) | Phase 1 (pl) | Scare events force player look direction |
| `pl.sens` read | Phase 5 (hide) | Phase 1 (pl) | Hiding system reads sensitivity for limited look |
| `pl.shake` write | Phase 6 (menu) | Phase 1 (pl) | Settings toggle disables camera animation |
| `pl.plavn` write | Phase 4 (wfplavn) | Phase 1 (pl) | One-shot smoothness override |
| `pl.enabled` write | Phase 5 (wfcode, wfzap, key) | Phase 1 (pl) | Disable player during interactions |
| `fl.enabled` write | Phase 5 (wfcode, wfzap, wfscare2v2) | Phase 1 (fl) | Disable flashlight during interactions |
| `cam (Animator).enabled` write | Phase 5 (hide, wfcode, wfzap) | Phase 1 (cam) | Disable camera bob during interactions |
| `vkl.use()` call | Phase 5 (trigscare) | Phase 2 (vkl) | Scare events toggle lights |
| `vkl.on` read | Phase 5 (trigscare), Phase 2 (tr) | Phase 2 (vkl) | Check if lights are on |
| `dver.enabled` write | Phase 5 (wfcode, key) | Phase 2 (dver) | Unlock door after puzzle/key |
| `dver.use()` call | Phase 5 (wfcode1) | Phase 2 (dver) | Event triggers door open |
| `lampa.x` write | Phase 5 (wfscare2) | Phase 2 (lampa) | Scare event changes lamp direction |
| `tryaska.enabled` write | Phase 3 (lift) | Phase 1 (tryaska) | Elevator enables camera shake |
| `lift.a()` call | Phase 3 (liftkn) | Phase 3 (lift) | Button → elevator |
| `nm.enabled` write | Phase 5 (wfkill) | Phase 5 (nm) | Kill sequence stops NavMesh |
| `shagi (AudioSource)` write | Phase 6 (menu) | Phase 1 (pl.shagi) | Pause silences footsteps |

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/wrngfloor/StructureMap.md ==== -->
# StructureMap — wrngfloor

## Naming Conventions

| Prefix | Meaning | Example |
|---|---|---|
| `SO_` | ScriptableObject (data definition) | `SO_DoorConfig` |
| `Field_` | SerializeField wrapper (inspector-editable) | `Field_InteractionDistance` |
| `W_` | Runtime wrapper (MonoBehaviour bridge) | `W_DoorAudio` |
| `I` | Interface (cross-system contract) | `IInteractable` |
| `DataService` | Pure C# logic (no MonoBehaviour) | `ElevatorStateMachine` |

---

## Phase 1 — Player Core

### `_-PlayerSystem/` (3+ tightly coupled files → system folder)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `pl.cs` | `PlayerController.cs` | Movement + Rigidbody force |
| `pl.cs` (camera part) | `PlayerLook.cs` | Mouse look, MX/MY/MZ, smoothing |
| `pl.cs` (audio part) | `W_PlayerFootsteps.cs` | Footstep audio volume/pitch |
| `cam.cs` | `InteractionRaycaster.cs` | Raycast + dispatch `IInteractable.Use()` |
| `fl.cs` | `FlashlightController.cs` | Flashlight hold, toggle, sway |
| `tryaska.cs` | `CameraShake.cs` | Screen shake effect |
| `lookat.cs` | `LookAtTarget.cs` | Utility — stays standalone |

**Interface Candidates:**
- `IInteractable` — replaces `SendMessage("use")` and name-based `GetComponent`. All interactable objects implement `void Use()`.
  ```csharp
  public interface IInteractable
  {
      void Use();
  }
  ```
- `IPlayerState` — read-only access to player position, look direction, sensitivity. Prevents direct `pl.GetComponent<pl>().MX` access.

**DataService Candidates:**
- `PlayerInputService` — pure C# class that reads Input axes and returns movement vector, look delta, button states. Extracted from `pl.Update()`.

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_PlayerConfig` — sensitivity, speed, run speed, FOV range, smoothing (plavn). Currently hardcoded in `pl.cs`.
- `SO_InteractionConfig` — raycast distance, layer masks. Currently fields on `cam.cs`.

---

## Phase 2 — Doors & Switches

### `_-DoorSystem/` (3+ tightly coupled files)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `dver.cs` | `PhysicsDoor.cs : IInteractable` | Hinge door with torque, slam detect |
| `wfdver1.cs` | `AnimatedDoor.cs : IInteractable` | Animation-driven door |
| `key.cs` | `KeyPickup.cs : IInteractable` | Key → unlocks a door |

**Interface Candidates:**
- `IDoor` — `void Unlock()`, `bool IsLocked` — shared by PhysicsDoor and AnimatedDoor.

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_DoorConfig` — torque value, angle thresholds (min/max/slmin/slmax), audio clips array. Currently all public fields on `dver.cs`.

### Standalone Interactables (no system folder needed)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `vkl.cs` | `LightSwitch.cs : IInteractable` | Switch with flicker |
| `vklt.cs` | `SimpleLightSwitch.cs : IInteractable` | Switch without flicker |
| `lampa.cs` | `AdjustableLamp.cs : IInteractable` | Rotatable lamp |
| `klych.cs` | `ObjectToggle.cs : IInteractable` | Activates/deactivates object arrays |
| `sound.cs` | `SoundTrigger.cs : IInteractable` | Plays audio on use |
| `tr.cs` | `ConditionalActivator.cs` | Activates target when switch is on |
| `wfpodsk.cs` | `HintPopup.cs : IInteractable` | Shows temporary UI hint |

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_LightSwitchConfig` — flicker min/max time, on/off objects. Currently inlined in `vkl.cs`.

---

## Phase 3 — Elevator System

### `_-ElevatorSystem/` (tightly coupled pair)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `lift.cs` (states 0-5) | `ElevatorController.cs` | Core elevator movement + door open/close |
| `lift.cs` (states 6-10) | `ElevatorSequence_Descent.cs` | Second descent + power-off sequence |
| `lift.cs` (states 20-23) | `ElevatorSequence_NPCReveal.cs` | NPC arrival + ending |
| `liftkn.cs` | `ElevatorButton.cs : IInteractable` | Button press triggers elevator |

**DataService Candidates:**
- `ElevatorStateMachine` — pure C# state machine with `enum ElevatorState`. Replaces raw `int x` field. Each state becomes a method or nested class.

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_ElevatorConfig` — speed, door lerp rate, floor heights, audio clips. Currently hardcoded magic numbers in `lift.cs`.

**Interface Candidates:**
- `IElevatorCallable` — `void Call()` — elevator button interface.

---

## Phase 4 — Environment & Optimization

### Standalone (all independent, no system folder needed)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `opt.cs` | `RoomCulling.cs` | Room activation manager |
| `opttrig.cs` | `RoomCullingTrigger.cs` | Zone trigger for room culling |
| `mirror.cs` | `MirrorReflection.cs` | Real-time mirror effect |
| `veter.cs` | `WindAudioFollower.cs` | Wind audio follows player Z |
| `audpitch.cs` | `DistancePitchController.cs` | Distance-based audio pitch |
| `wfplavn.cs` | `PlayerSmoothnessOverride.cs` | One-shot smoothness set |
| `kadr25.cs` | `FrameRateCameraSwap.cs` | Horror low-FPS camera effect |
| `Wftpscam.cs` | `ThirdPersonDeathCam.cs` | Wall-collision third-person camera |

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_RoomCullingConfig` — room list + initial states. Currently arrays on `opt.cs`.

---

## Phase 5 — Horror Events & NPC

### `_-NPCSystem/` (3 tightly coupled files)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `nm.cs` | `NPCWalker.cs` | NavMesh walk to waypoint |
| `wfkill.cs` | `NPCKillSequence.cs` | Detect player → kill animation → game over |
| `wfscare1.cs` | `NPCScareEvent.cs` | NPC animates on player sight |

### `_-PuzzleSystem/` (3 tightly coupled files)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `wfcode.cs` | `CombinationLock.cs : IInteractable` | 4-cylinder code puzzle |
| `wfzap.cs` | `LockInspection.cs : IInteractable` | Camera zoom to examine lock |
| `hide.cs` | `HidingSpot.cs : IInteractable` | Player hide in furniture |

### `_-ScareEventSystem/` (3+ scripted scare types)

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `wfscare2.cs` | `ScareEvent_NPCAppear.cs` | NPC appears, animates on trigger |
| `wfscare2v2.cs` | `ScareEvent_ForcedLook.cs` | Force player to look at NPC |
| `addforcescr.cs` | `ScareEvent_DoorSlam.cs` | Door slams with FOV flash |
| `trigscare.cs` | `ScareEvent_LightsOut.cs` | Lights off + NPC animation |
| `wfcode1.cs` | `ScareEvent_WrongFloor.cs` | Ambient horror sequence |
| `golova.cs` | `SkullInspection.cs : IInteractable` | Head examination |

### Standalone

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `f.cs` | `FlashlightPuzzle.cs` | Toggle light reveals hidden objects |
| `f2.cs` | `DarknessFearEffect.cs` | Voice + heartbeat when light off |
| `wfsatr.cs` | `TriggerActivator.cs` | Activate/deactivate on trigger enter |
| `wfcolis.cs` | `CollisionPopup.cs` | Show popup on collision |
| `wftryaska.cs` | `WorldObjectShake.cs` | Object shake + LookAt |

**DataService Candidates:**
- `CombinationLockLogic` — pure C# class with `int[] digits`, `bool Check(int[] code)`, `void IncrementDigit(int index, int direction)`. Extracted from `wfcode.cs` input handling.

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_CombinationLockConfig` — correct code digits, cylinder count, input delay. Hardcoded as `1990` in `wfcode.cs`.
- `SO_ScareEventConfig` — timing values, FOV snap values, audio clips per scare event.

**Interface Candidates:**
- `IScareEvent` — `void Trigger()`, `bool HasTriggered` — standardizes scare event lifecycle.

### Standalone

| Source File | Target Structure | Role |
|---|---|---|
| `menu.cs` | `PauseMenu.cs` | Pause, settings, language, quit |

**SO Candidates:**
- `SO_GameSettings` — runtime settings (sensitivity, volume, language, shake toggle). Currently written directly to `pl` fields and `AudioListener`.

## Summary: Interface Map

| Interface | Implementors | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `IInteractable` | PhysicsDoor, AnimatedDoor, KeyPickup, LightSwitch, SimpleLightSwitch, AdjustableLamp, ObjectToggle, SoundTrigger, HintPopup, CombinationLock, LockInspection, HidingSpot, SkullInspection, ElevatorButton | Replaces SendMessage("use") |
| `IDoor` | PhysicsDoor, AnimatedDoor | Shared lock/unlock contract |
| `IScareEvent` | All scare event scripts | Standardized trigger lifecycle |
| `IPlayerState` | PlayerController | Read-only player state for external systems |

## Summary: DataService Map

| DataService | Extracted From | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| `PlayerInputService` | `pl.cs` | Pure input reading |
| `ElevatorStateMachine` | `lift.cs` | State machine logic |
| `CombinationLockLogic` | `wfcode.cs` | Puzzle validation |

## Summary: SO Map

| ScriptableObject | Replaces | Fields |
|---|---|---|
| `SO_PlayerConfig` | Hardcoded values in `pl.cs` | sens, speed, runSpeed, fovMin/Max, plavn |
| `SO_InteractionConfig` | Fields on `cam.cs` | dist, layerMask |
| `SO_DoorConfig` | Fields on `dver.cs` | torque, angleMin/Max, slamThresholds, audioClips |
| `SO_LightSwitchConfig` | Fields on `vkl.cs` | flickerMinTime, flickerMaxTime, objectArrays |
| `SO_ElevatorConfig` | Magic numbers in `lift.cs` | speed, doorLerpRate, floorHeights, audioClips |
| `SO_CombinationLockConfig` | Hardcoded in `wfcode.cs` | correctCode, cylinderCount, inputDelay |
| `SO_GameSettings` | Direct writes in `menu.cs` | sensitivity, volume, language, shakeEnabled |

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/wrngfloor/SystemPortabilityMap.md ==== -->
# SystemPortabilityMap — wrngfloor

## Portability Levels

| Level | Definition |
|---|---|
| **L0** | Project-specific — tightly coupled to wrngfloor scene, hardcoded positions/values, not reusable |
| **L1** | Configurable — could work in another project with SO config changes, minor refactoring |
| **L2** | Portable — generic system, drop into any Unity project with minimal wiring |

---

## Classification

### L2 — Portable (drop-in reusable)

| Script | Target Name | Why Portable |
|---|---|---|
| `lookat.cs` | `LookAtTarget` | Generic LookAt — zero project coupling |
| `tryaska.cs` | `CameraShake` | Generic shake — parameterized random rotation |
| `audpitch.cs` | `DistancePitchController` | Generic distance→pitch — works anywhere |
| `sound.cs` | `SoundTrigger` | Generic audio player on use |
| `klych.cs` | `ObjectToggle` | Generic activate/deactivate arrays |
| `wfpodsk.cs` | `HintPopup` | Generic timed popup — any UI |
| `wfsatr.cs` | `TriggerActivator` | Generic trigger zone → activate/deactivate |
| `wfcolis.cs` | `CollisionPopup` | Generic collision → popup |
| `opt.cs` | `RoomCulling` | Generic room activation manager |
| `opttrig.cs` | `RoomCullingTrigger` | Generic zone-based room culling |
| `veter.cs` | `WindAudioFollower` | Generic audio position follower (Z-axis) |
| `wftryaska.cs` | `WorldObjectShake` | Generic object shake + LookAt |
| `kadr25.cs` | `FrameRateCameraSwap` | Generic frame-rate camera alternation |

### L1 — Configurable (reusable with SO/config changes)

| Script | Target Name | What Needs Config |
|---|---|---|
| `pl.cs` | `PlayerController` + `PlayerLook` | Speed, sensitivity, FOV range → SO_PlayerConfig |
| `cam.cs` | `InteractionRaycaster` | Distance, layer mask → SO_InteractionConfig. IInteractable interface makes it generic. |
| `fl.cs` | `FlashlightController` | Sway parameters, light settings → configurable |
| `dver.cs` | `PhysicsDoor` | Torque, angles, audio → SO_DoorConfig |
| `vkl.cs` | `LightSwitch` | Flicker timing → SO_LightSwitchConfig |
| `vklt.cs` | `SimpleLightSwitch` | Already generic, just needs IInteractable |
| `lampa.cs` | `AdjustableLamp` | Rotation presets → could be SO |
| `key.cs` | `KeyPickup` | Generic if door reference is via IDoor |
| `nm.cs` | `NPCWalker` | Generic NavMesh walk — just needs waypoint |
| `hide.cs` | `HidingSpot` | Camera positions/limits → configurable |
| `menu.cs` | `PauseMenu` | Bindings → SO_GameSettings |
| `mirror.cs` | `MirrorReflection` | Generic mirror math — targets configurable |
| `Wftpscam.cs` | `ThirdPersonDeathCam` | Generic wall-clip camera |
| `tr.cs` | `ConditionalActivator` | Generic conditional on vkl.on → could generalize to any bool source |

### L0 — Project-Specific (tied to wrngfloor)

| Script | Target Name | Why L0 |
|---|---|---|
| `lift.cs` | `ElevatorController` | 23-state machine with hardcoded positions (y=3.33242, y=-3, y=-4.73), specific NPC reveal sequence, specific floor layout |
| `liftkn.cs` | `ElevatorButton` | Trivially generic, but semantically part of elevator system |
| `wfcode.cs` | `CombinationLock` | Code 1990 hardcoded, specific cylinder meshes/materials, specific door reference |
| `wfcode1.cs` | `ScareEvent_WrongFloor` | Hardcoded x/z position checks (22.8, 6.5, 22, 19.1), specific object references |
| `wfkill.cs` | `NPCKillSequence` | Specific NPC + death camera + scene-specific destruction |
| `wfscare1.cs` | `NPCScareEvent` | Hardcoded timing (1.75s), forced look angles (-90, 10), specific NPC |
| `wfscare2.cs` | `ScareEvent_NPCAppear` | Hardcoded z-position triggers (3.5, 4.0), specific lamp reference |
| `wfscare2v2.cs` | `ScareEvent_ForcedLook` | Hardcoded position checks (17.5, 18.0), forced look angles (270, 10) |
| `addforcescr.cs` | `ScareEvent_DoorSlam` | Generic-ish but has specific force values and FOV flash sequence |
| `trigscare.cs` | `ScareEvent_LightsOut` | Hardcoded position (-1.7, -2.02, 2.56), specific vkl/cam coupling |
| `golova.cs` | `SkullInspection` | Specific head/eye/camera setup |
| `f.cs` | `FlashlightPuzzle` | Specific reveal sequence (4 objects) |
| `f2.cs` | `DarknessFearEffect` | Specific heartbeat/voice timing |
| `wfplavn.cs` | `PlayerSmoothnessOverride` | One-shot destroy — specific value 10f |
| `wfdver1.cs` | `AnimatedDoor` | Specific animation trigger "a" |

---

## Migration Priority

**Migrate L2 scripts first** — they are the easiest wins and establish patterns.
**Migrate L1 scripts second** — they become L2 once SO configs are extracted.
**L0 scripts last** — they require the most project-specific knowledge and will stay somewhat coupled to the scene.

| Priority | Count | Action |
|---|---|---|
| 1st | 13 L2 scripts | Rename, add IInteractable, done |
| 2nd | 14 L1 scripts | Rename, extract SO config, add interfaces |
| 3rd | 15 L0 scripts | Refactor with DataServices, extract hardcoded values to SO where possible |

<!-- ==== FILE: LEARN/wrngfloor/surfer.md ==== -->
# surfer — wrngfloor

## Prompt 1: Initial source analysis

**Date:** 2025-05-16

**Action:** Full project initialization — read all 38 game scripts in `MAIN-SOURCE/wrngfloor/Scripts/Assembly-CSharp/`, analyzed .stub file (11,211 files, 765 MB), mapped dependency graph, identified god objects and coupling hotspots.

**Key Findings:**
- Horror first-person game, Unity HDRP, single scene (174 MB)
- 38 actionable game scripts, all extend MonoBehaviour directly (flat hierarchy)
- Zero events/interfaces — all coupling via direct references + SendMessage
- `cam.cs` uses fragile name-based GetComponent dispatch
- `pl.cs` is the most depended-on script (20+ dependents)
- `lift.cs` is the largest/most complex (23-state elevator machine)
- No singletons, no ScriptableObjects, no save system
- Heavy GetComponent calls in Update (uncached)
- Russian-named variables throughout (dver=door, shagi=footsteps, vkl=switch, etc.)

**Generated:**
- ARCHITECTURE.md — full dependency graph, coupling hotspots, asset inventory
- PhaseMap.md — 6 phases, 41 files, cross-phase modification table
- StructureMap.md — system folders, interfaces, DataServices, SOs per phase
- GOAL.md — architecture rules, naming conventions, decoupling patterns, migration order
- Estimate.md — 20h code + 8h overhead = 28h total
- SystemPortabilityMap.md — 13 L2 (portable), 14 L1 (configurable), 15 L0 (project-specific)
